GridPlot in Bokeh¶

DataFrame aware linked axis exploration of a dataframe.

In [1]:
    %load_ext literacy
In [2]:
    import pandas as pd; from bokeh import plotting, models, resources, layouts
    plotting.output_notebook()

import pandas as pd; from bokeh import plotting, models, resources, layouts
plotting.output_notebook()

    df = pd.util.testing.makeDataFrame().reset_index(drop=True)
  • Use pandas testing data for the demostration.
df = pd.util.testing.makeDataFrame().reset_index(drop=True)
In [4]:
* Make a widget for each features column; use the widget to store column metadata.

---
    
    controls = {_: models.Slider(
        value=10, start=10, end=1000, step=2, title=_
    ) for _ in df.columns}
  • Make a widget for each features column; use the widget to store column metadata.
controls = {_: models.Slider(
    value=10, start=10, end=1000, step=2, title=_
) for _ in df.columns}
In [5]:
* Initialize diagonal data sources; ATM the widgets won't change anything.  

> * these should be able to update on the client
> * Perform a value counts binning operation for this demonstration.

    diagonals = {}
    for _ in controls:
        bins = pd.np.linspace(df[_].min(), df[_].max(), controls[_].value)
        diagonals[_] = df[_].apply(
            pd.np.digitize, args=(bins,)
        ).value_counts().sort_index().to_frame(_).rename(dict(zip(range(1, len(bins)+1), bins))).pipe(plotting.ColumnDataSource)
  • Initialize diagonal data sources; ATM the widgets won't change anything.
  • these should be able to update on the client
  • Perform a value counts binning operation for this demonstration.
diagonals = {}
for _ in controls:
    bins = pd.np.linspace(df[_].min(), df[_].max(), controls[_].value)
    diagonals[_] = df[_].apply(
        pd.np.digitize, args=(bins,)
    ).value_counts().sort_index().to_frame(_).rename(dict(zip(range(1, len(bins)+1), bins))).pipe(plotting.ColumnDataSource)
